        <h2>
         <a href="/story/2014/07/07/1312240/-After-free-contraception-program-Colorado-teen-birth-rate-plummets" id="titleHref">
          After free contraception program, Colorado teen birth rate plummets
         </a>
         <span style="white-space: nowrap">
         </span>
        </h2>
        <p class="author">
         <span>
          by
         </span>
         <a href="/user/Jen Hayden">
          Jen Hayden
         </a>
         <a alt="Follow this author" class="ajax type-user do-hotlist do-updateContent size-tiny off altTooltip" href="#?friend_id=41648&amp;is_stream=1">
          Follow
         </a>
        </p>
        <ul class="front-page-share clearfix">
         <li style="margin-left: 0px">
          <div class="fb-share-button" data-href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/07/07/1312240/-After-free-contraception-program-Colorado-teen-birth-rate-plummets" data-layout="button_count">
          </div>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="twitter-share-button" data-count="horizontal" data-related="markos" data-text="After free contraception program, Colorado teen birth rate plummets" data-url="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/07/07/1312240/-After-free-contraception-program-Colorado-teen-birth-rate-plummets" data-via="dailykos" href="https://twitter.com/share">
           Tweet
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="comments comment_count_with_new" data-comment_count="106" data-story_id="1312240" href="/story/2014/07/07/1312240/-After-free-contraception-program-Colorado-teen-birth-rate-plummets#comments">
           106 Comments
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <div class="article-body">
        <div id="intro">
         <div class="dkimg-c">
          <span class="image_container">
           <img alt="Birth control pill" height="462" src="http://images.dailykos.com/images/93195/large/pill.jpg?1404740781" width="550"/>
          </span>
         </div>
         <iframe defang_overflow="false" frameborder="0" height="375" src="https://dailykos.com/campaigns/884.embed" style="box-shadow: 0px 3px 10px 6px #EBEBEB;margin: 0px 15px 10px 15px;float:right;" width="275">
         </iframe>
         <p>
          Outstanding news
          <a href="http://www.denverpost.com/news/ci_26085784/colorado-teen-birth-rates-drop-state-hands-out?ok">
           in Colorado:
          </a>
          <br/>
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          A state health initiative to reduce teen birth rates by providing more than 30,000 contraceptive devices at low or no cost has led to a 40 percent drop in five years, Gov. John Hickenlooper said Thursday.
          <p>
           The Colorado Family Planning Initiative, funded by a private anonymous donor for five years, has provided intrauterine devices and other implants to low-income women at 68 family-planning clinics across Colorado since 2009.
          </p>
          <p>
           The clinics are in local health departments, hospitals and private nonprofit facilities. The program also provided training and technical assistance to family planning clinics statewide.
          </p>
          <p>
           "When families are planned and women have children when they're ready and want them ... it's really a better situation for everyone," Hickenlooper said during his state Capitol news conference.
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         What a novel idea! It's cost-saving for the state of Colorado
         <a href="http://www.colorado.gov/cs/Satellite/CDPHE-PSD/CBON/1251618366665">
          as well:
         </a>
         <br/>
         <blockquote>
          Costs to Colorados Economy: Unintended pregnancy burdens Colorados health and economy, costing Colorado more than $160 million annually in Medicaid expenditures. Nationally, for every public dollar spent on family planning services, $3.74 is saved in Medicaid costs for pregnancy-related services and newborn care.
         </blockquote>
        </div>
        <p class="divider-doodle">
        </p>

         <div class="tooltipContents qtip-style-dk4_large qtip-pos-br">
          <p>
           <b>
            More Tagging tips:
           </b>
          </p>
          <p>
           A tag is a way to search for this diary. If someone is searching for "Barack Obama," is this a diary they'd be trying to find?
          </p>
          <p>
           Use a person's full name, without any title. Senator Obama may become President Obama, and Michelle Obama might run for office.
          </p>
          <p>
           If your diary covers an election or elected official, use election tags, which are generally the state abbreviation followed by the office. 
		CA-01 is the first district House seat. CA-Sen covers both senate races. NY-GOV covers the New York governor's race.
          </p>
          <p>
           Tags do not compound: that is, "education reform" is a completely different tag from "education". A tag like "reform" alone is probably not meaningful.
          </p>

          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Education');return false;">

          </a>

          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('White House');return false;">

          </a>
          .
	If your diary is specific to a state, consider adding the state 
	(
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('California');return false;">
           California
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Texas');return false;">
           Texas
          </a>
          , etc).
	Keep in mind, though, that there are many wonderful and important diaries
	that don't fit in any of these tags. Don't worry if yours doesn't.

             </p>
             <p>
              Aside from the fact that this problem contributes to lack of jobs for all, we are running out of resources such as usable land and water. This is a worse problem in the Southwest as we are experiencing drought. But even without drought, places like LA and Las Vegas would simply not be sustainable without stealing water from hundreds of miles away. And those water supplies are dwindling.
             </p>
             <p>
              Although we have plenty of land still available in the US, much of it is desert and unusable because of lack of water. And things could get far worse with global warming.
             </p>
             <p>
              I am not a Christian anymore but I am familiar with the Bible and I am not sure where the Catholic church gets its policies on birth control. I know there is a passage in the OT where a man was punished for "spilling his seed". But the context is that in ancient Judaism a widow was required to marry her brother-in-law in order to be taken care of and further the family line. It was the brother-in-law who was required to essentially make children FOR HIS DEAD BROTHER. So in this particular instance the man was punished by God for failing to fulfill this duty.
             </p>
             <p>
              Unless the Pope wants to reinstate a widow marrying her brother-in-law (most likely resulting in polygamy too, since the man probably already would have a wife.) then I really don't think he has a leg to stand on theologically.
             </p>
             <p>
              Fortunately the Catholic church cannot control people as easilly as it used to because more people are literate and can interprete things themselves. A lot of American Catholics simply ignore that teaching. Hopefully that will eventually rub off onto the illegals as well. But will that happen quickly enough?
             </p>
             <p>
              In a world with 7 billion people and growing exponentially we simply cannot afford to keep going down this road.
             </p>
             <p>
              This was the world population when I was born in 1964: 3,263,738,832 at a 2.00% annual growth rate.
             </p>
             <p>
              This is what it is projected for 2064 at a modest 0.32% annual growth rate: 10,094,674,166
             </p>
             <p>
              In 2014 we are at a 1.12% annual growth rate which is better but not nearly good enough.
             </p>
             <p>
              (source: UN, Dept. of Economic and Social Affairs, Population Division (2013).)
             </p>
             <p>
              The Pope, IF HE IS COURAGEOUS ENOUGH can make a difference. I don't give a damn about doctrine and tradition. Overpopulation is one of the biggest causes of misery and poverty in the world.
              <strong>
               If he is serious about alieviating suffering in the world than this is his litmus test!
               <br/>
              </strong>
             </p>
            </div>

            <li id="c89">
             <div class="cx" id="cx53894525">
              <h5>
               <a class="de">
               </a>
               <span class="cu">
                You are right that many teens wait, but for a
               </span>
               <span class="crd ntb">
                (
                <a href="/comments/1312240/53894525#c89?mode=alone;showrate=1#c89">
                 0+ / 0-
                </a>
                )
               </span>
              </h5>
              <div class="ct">
               <p>
                significant portion of those, it is just because the opportunity never arose for one reason or another. Those who deny that teens have sex because they
                <em>
                 want
                </em>
                to are denying biology. Every other species begins mating as soon as they are sexually mature. Why should we believe that humans are any different? The biological drive is there, and teens are not particularly good at impulse control. We can try to talk our kids out of having sex until they are more mature, but it is good to also arm them with knowledge of how the body works and how to
                <em>
                 not
                </em>
                become pregnant or catch an STD.
               </p>
              </div>
              <div class="cf">
               <p class="sig">
                Republicans - A pathology, not a party.
               </p>
               <p class="cb">
                by
                <a href="/user/uid:974986">
                 storeysound
                </a>
                on
                <a href="/comments/1312240/53894525#c89">
                 Wed Jul 09, 2014 at 12:46:41 PM PDT
                </a>
               </p>
               <p class="cl">
                [
                <a href="#c48">
                 Parent
                </a>

              </div>
             </div>
            </li>
            <ul class="cm i1" id="k53894525">
             <li id="c100">
              <div class="cx" id="cx56493532">
               <h5>
                <a class="de">
                </a>
                <span class="cu">
                 some teens wait
                </span>
                <span class="crd ntb">
                 (
                 <a href="/comments/1312240/56493532#c100?mode=alone;showrate=1#c100">
                  0+ / 0-
                 </a>
                 )
                </span>
               </h5>
               <div class="ct">
                <p>
                 for a variety of reasons. Fear that birth control might fail, for one. Not being conventionally attractive. Fear of losing out on educational or career opportunities. Not wanting to risk being stuck in their parents' house any longer than necessary. Concerns about the pain of sex and/or childbirth. A belief that sex connects you to the other person in a permanent way, even if the relationship ends. Fear of encountering an aggressive or abusive partner. Admiration for someone who credits waiting with other opportunities they have enjoyed. . . .
                </p>
                <p>
                 Or some combination. I'm sure other people could add other reasons to that list.
                </p>
                <p>
                 I always assumed that sex created a particular type of psychological connection to a person, and that that would confound to some extent, subsequent relationships unless the participant deemphasized the importance of sex to them. But doing so would mean that the importance of the sexual relationship wouldn't be there to reinforce a more important relationship at a later date, and I didn't want to be comparing a future spouse to a bunch of past lovers, each of whom may have excelled at one part of the physical and/or emotional aspects of being in a relationship. So, while I didn't wait until I was married, I did minimize those external comparisons to a couple of people who I believed met all of the important criteria I had when looking for a long-term partner.
                </p>
                <p>
                 In retrospect, I don't know whether it was a valid concern, as I never found a partner with a similar history, but it did mean that I wasn't sexually active at a particularly young age. So whether from fear, social pressure, or reasoning from a position of limited information, there are a lot of reasons some people wait.
                </p>
                <p>
                 I agree that arming them with the most complete biological information is the only response that makes sense though.
                </p>
               </div>

           <div class="cx" id="cx53878317">
            <h5>
             <a class="de">
             </a>
             <span class="cu">
              We never waited.
             </span>
             <span class="crd ntb">
              (
              <a href="/comments/1312240/53878317#c53?mode=alone;showrate=1#c53">
               5+ / 0-

            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              What makes you think they will? Should we have waited? glad I didn't. Wish I had gotten over my Catholic shame sooner. Wish someone had explained it as a normal part of life, in all its sprawling aspects..
             </p>
             <p>
              We need to get over ourselves. Hurling aging frames into the stampede of youth in a frantic effort to deflect it is what we laughed at our parents for.
             </p>
             <p>
              My grandparents (born around 1900) lived the Roaring 20s with gangsters, flappers and movies that routinely showed abortions, drug use, kept women, gays and nudity. Great Gatsby and the Harlem Renaissance. Prohibition. Free love. They were no innocents. My parents WWII generation cleaned it up for the kids.
             </p>
             <p>
              This generation reminds me a lot of their experiences.
             </p>
             <p>
              We didn't invent sex. Neither did your parents. We survived.
             </p>
             <p>
              Teach your children well.  Remember: they have the web.....any 5 year old can Google 'SEX.' And probably has.
             </p>

             <h5>
              <a class="de">
              </a>
              <span class="cu">
               And lest we forget, many (particularly girls) of
              </span>
              <span class="crd ntb">
               (
               <a href="/comments/1312240/53894688#c90?mode=alone;showrate=1#c90">
                0+ / 0-
               </a>
               )
              </span>
             </h5>
             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               our grandparents' and great-grandparents' generations were marrying and having kids (not necessarily in that order) at the age of 16 or 17, as has been the case throughout human history. Delaying marriage, and, theoretically, sex and child-bearing until the late teens or twenties is a very recent development, and coincided with the increasing access to college and the general workforce in the early part of the 20th Century, and accelerated with so many women entering the workforce during WWII.
              </p>

          <li id="c70">
           <div class="cx" id="cx53880708">
            <h5>
             <a class="de">
             </a>
             <span class="cu">
              I have often wondered why the body grows up
             </span>
             <span class="crd ntb">
              (
              <a href="/comments/1312240/53880708#c70?mode=alone;showrate=1#c70">
               2+ / 0-
              </a>
              )
             </span>
            </h5>
            <div class="crs">
             <dl>
              <dt>
               Recommended by:
              </dt>
              <dd>
               <a href="/user/uid:197517">
                NotActingNaive
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:896132">
                VPofKarma
               </a>
              </dd>
             </dl>
            </div>
            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              faster than the brain. The brain does not fully mature until around age 25. That is why kids make stupid choices because the part of the brain dealing with consequences is undeveloped.
             </p>
             <p>
              My guess is that evolutionary-wise it didn't matter in tribal cultures because children were raised communally. So the more mature adults helped in the raising instead of having children raising children.
             </p>
             <p>
              However there is another possibility. Neural plasticity. In most tribal cultures they prepare children for adulthood through ritual and initiation bestowing greater responsibility on them around the age of 13. Is it possible that that somehow affects how the brain develops?
             </p>
             <p>
              Our extended childhood to accomodate education has created many problems because in more "primitive" cultures sexual activity started much younger.
             </p>
             <p>
              Yes it is better to wait but preparedness makes sense. Even in the "good old days" when pre-marital sex was frowned upon, we still had a problem with teenage pregnancy. It was just hidden better.
             </p>
            </div>

           </p>
           <p>
            Male Birth Control: New Procedure Is 100 Percent Effective, Reversible..
           </p>
           <p>
            The whole procedure takes about 15 minutes and lasts ten years or more and is more easily reversible than a vasectomy.
           </p>
           <p>
            As the Male Contraception Information Project notes, if a man decides he'd like to have his sperm up and running again, he can get another shot and, within two to three months, the baby-making can commence.
           </p>
           <p>
            Studies over the last 25 years have reportedly found the procedure is safe to use on both humans and animals.
           </p>
           <p>
            Researchers are hopeful that the procedure will be on the market in the U.S. by 2015, with clinical trials beginning in 2012.
           </p>

           </p>
           <p>
            How on earth did the Colorado Family Planning Initiative ever make it past the Republican Sex and Morality Police? Why has this program failed to draw the attention, anger and condemnation of the busybody Bible-thumpers on the Christian Right? Although it was funded for five years by a private, anonymous donor, you can bet that the conservatives will try like hell to shut down this sorely-needed, rational, realistic initiative.
           </p>
           <p>
            A 40% drop in teenage pregnancies and savings on health care costs mean zilch to the right-wing lunatics who are hellbent for leather on denying women access to any forms of birth control. Statistics and sensibility? Those nut jobs don't need no steenking statistics and sensibility, anything that could keep them from going off the deep end on the subject of pregnancy prevention. Fucking dolts.

  <script type="text/javascript">
   if($.cookie('meter_user') !== 'false') {
		if ($('#ePostButton').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('#ePostButton').click(function() { 
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Posted Comment', { 
		      repliedTo: $(this).parents('#eP').prevAll('.cb').children('a').first().html() 
		    });
		  });
		}
		
		if (!!document.location.pathname.match('activate') &amp;&amp; $('h1:contains("Welcome to Daily Kos!")').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Signed Up');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname === '/') {
		  if (document.location.hostname.match(/^www|^dailykos/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Front Page');
		  } else {
		    var subdomain = document.location.hostname.split('.')[0];
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Vertical', { name: subdomain });
		  }
		}
		
		if ($('.ratinate').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.ratinate').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Comment') });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-addRating.type-story').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-addRating.type-story').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Story') });
		}
		
		if ($("form[action$='publishHow']").length &gt; 0) {
		  $(document).ready(function() {
			  $('.type-story.do-publishHow').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Published Story') });
			 });
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/user/) &amp;&amp; $('li.here').length &gt; 0) {
		  if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Stream/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Stream', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Profile/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Profile', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:last li.here').children('a').html().match(/My Recent Replies/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Replies');
		  }
		} 
		
		if ($('#search-tabbed').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Searched');
		}
		
		if ($('#group-tables').length &gt; 0) {
			DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Groups List');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/groups/) &amp;&amp; $("#group_info").length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Group', { name: $('.name').children('a').text() });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').click(function() {
		    var nickName;
		    nickName = ($(this).prev('a').html() || $('.name a').html())
		    if ($(this).hasClass('do-hotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Followed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    } else if ($(this).hasClass('do-unHotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Unfollowed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    }    
		  });
		}
	}
  </script>
